Oh, my children, now that I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, through its completion and the end it brings, and by its explanations and declarations, it is evident to me that I complete for you here this treatise, which is part of surgical operation, so it is surgery.
Since the operation of surgery is prohibited in our region and in our times, yet it is a science that should not be neglected, and its principles are well-known; and only some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients have survived, which correct many errors and hesitations among them, thus understanding of it has diminished and its force and art have been weakened.
And it is clear to me that I should vitalize that part of this treatise in accordance with the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and so that it comes in line with the forms of the surgical instruments, including their addition by declaration and preparation, which is necessary for the cause.
More than that, the reason why a good artisan does not apply his hand in this our time is that the art of medicine is long and difficult, and one must be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen knew well, knowing the youth of the members and their forms, the joints and separation of them; and had knowledge of the bones, the nerves, and the arteries, their number and their properties; and of the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their contraction and expansion.
And for this, Hippocrates is said to have named it "Mot," but in his smaller work, more so in the art of the hand.
More than that, we have already spoken of this in the introduction to this book; for those who do not know what we have said about anatomy will fall into error on this account, which will cause men to die, as I have seen too many of them. For some are formed in this science but proceed from the other sciences and their experiments.
For I have seen a foolish and inexperienced doctor who caused an apostematosis escrophularia in the neck of a woman, and severed some arteries in the neck so that much blood flowed, and the woman died from this.
And there was another doctor who almost drained a stone from a man who had been suffering from his condition, and the stone was large, and it came to him, and he drained that stone with a piece of the bladder, so that man died on the third day.
And I have already called for the stone to be removed, and I see that due to the size of the stone and the condition of the patient lying there, he will die.
And there was another doctor who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he came upon a black slave who had suffered a fracture in the thigh; and due to the doctor's ignorance, he removed the fracture, over the wound, with pillows and splints of strong structure, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then the dislocation according to his desires, and then the reattachment, and then let it rest for a few days as commanded that we release the ligament; and thus remain so until the thigh and foot are fully healed, and only then proceed.
And I was called to him, and prepared to untie the ligament, and success brought peace and an attempt to relieve his pains.
But nonetheless, since corruption was confirmed in the member, I could not prevent it, and did not cease to circulate the corruption in the member while the illness persisted.
And there was another doctor who incised an oncotic abscess, and it ulcerated for several days, during which the malignity of the illness increased in the lord.
The cause is that the pain is purely of melancholic humor, and does not affect the whole body, but rather affects a member which suffers from being assailed by it.
And for this reason, my children, it is necessary for you that the operation be devised in two ways: one where the operation is associated with health, and one where the work is perilous in the major preparations.
And I have already existed in all parts of this book in which the operation is filled with error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to guard this and leave that, so that the leaves do not find a way to speak ill of you.

And therefore it is said that the cautery comforts all kinds of universal ailments which are either in flesh or sinew, except for two kinds, which are gout ailments.

Capitol.xl.
In which the main discussion on abscesses and their treatment is presented.
Abscesses are special lumps, of various kinds, according to their nature, and each one in this treatise.
And they are diverse in puncturing and treating them through two methods. One method is specifically for abscesses themselves; the other is for what is compressed by the humors.
And the second method is near the places where bodily accidents occur, for an abscess in the head is different from an abscess in the buttocks; and an abscess in a fleshy area is different from an abscess in a joint; and each one of them has its own judgment through operation.
And for abscesses some of which cover areas that should not be perforated but rather allowed to mature until the healing is complete in those areas.
So for other abscesses which must be incised when they are ripe and not matured according to their completion, thus for abscesses that are near joints, when an abscess is near a joint, its nature extends into what is within the circuit of the joint, and corrupts the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing contraction of that limb; or if it is an abscess near the main limb, and you delay the incision until it matures naturally in the main limb; or if it is near the anus, therefore incise what is not yet ripe; and should not be cut raw due to poor digestion, but one near the anus, so that it does not become inflamed and extend inward into the parts of the anus, causing a fistula, or done at a time when it is not healed. You must know the time for incising the abscess, and this is when it is ripe.
And know that it is matured when there is the cessation of pain and the end of fever, and then the decrease in redness and pulse, and the subsiding sharpness at the head of the boil, and other signs.
And know when to puncture the abscess in the location near it and allow the pus from the swelling to drain.
And the puncturing should be done along the length of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the thigh or foot, and at the location of the lacertae, the cords of the nerves, the arches; and, finally, in all locations where there is no reflection; for in those that do reflect, use puncturing according to that member.
When the abscess is in flesh, it is better to delay the puncturing until the digestion of it is confirmed according to complement, as we have said; for if you puncture it too soon, it will prolong the course of the pus and misthick the walls of it so they become more hardened and deep.
More abscesses should be perforated according to the width of the flesh or body if necessary, or according to that from which the member suffers.
And ensure that you administer a small perforation in large abscesses, or a large and wide opening or multiple sections according to the size of the abscesses.
And in other abscesses, ensure that the cord is returned to its cavity and tied, when this is done as if with a bandage or string, do it thoroughly, just as you would in cases of tumors and buboes.
And of those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those in which the incision is made as the figure of a mint leaf, as with abscesses of phlyax.
And of these, those in which a round section and a lunar section are administered, similar to those.
More so for those in which no such thing is done, as with superficial abscesses of lions, ensure that you perforate them with a superficial or flat perforation only.
And when the abscess is large and has collected much healthy pus, that you puncture it and do not hesitate to extract all the purulent matter at that time; having extracted one part, then on another day incise the abscess further, extracting a larger portion, and proceed in this manner making punctures according to degree until it is fully evacuated.
And especially if the patient is of strong virtue, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an old person in decline, for the animal spirit has resolved into the exit of the healthy matter, and greatly alleviates the illness, and you may openly perform.
Take great care with this chapter, and when you perform your puncture on these abscesses, ensure that you cleanse the wounds and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small or if it forms a flat section. Then administer either hot or cold applications accordingly; if the abscess is large and the openings from the puncture are painful, then place your hand in each to ensure they heal together.
And if in the abscess you have separated a part of the cord or have concave it in the circuit, then you should close it with cold flax or with a thread made of linen cloth, just as when you have drawn out blood or roots, to maintain their humidity; strengthen it on the seventh day; and proceed with it and cure it according to what is appropriate with ointments until it is healed.
But if you should happen to have a flow of blood during the hour of your operation, then administer water infused with wine in which you soak a cloth, and place that over the location of the bleeding several times.
But if the flow of blood persists, then you should administer treatment and cure with powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and division.
But if it is in the time of winter, and the location of the abscess is near major nerves, then you should infuse powders with wine and oil, and place those over the areas.
And if it is in the summer, and the areas are fleshy, then you should place powders infused in water and oil or in wine and oil, and all of this be steeped for three days, as we have said, and then you should incise the abscess, cleanse it, and administer to it whatever is appropriate for its cure until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary concerning the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the division I have already said about all abscesses in what manner the cure of each one is treated individually.
Chapter XL.
Of the section on abscesses that occur in the chain of the head.
In the chain of the head, small abscesses occur, and these contain nodules which are formed by their own tissues; the nature of these nodules is spotted.
And they are lumps, and among them are those that contain humidity resembling lime. And among them are those that contain humidity resembling dust, similar to it; and among them are those that are hard and calcified.
And in the section of all of them, and in the extraction of those, there should be no fear, just as you should not fear the extraction of those without.
And the operation for the section of these is that you express them with an instrument in the form of which see below, which is called a lancet, until you know it contains pus.

On Hernia Ventosa.
In this hernia, it is not seen that anything has been burnt during the treatment of the wound.
And the first doctors said that it should be done as we have recommended in the hernia that is present; which is that you tie the vessels near the section over which there is ease; and then dry out the middle part by applying a poultice with what operates on it, so that the vessels may fall.
And cure the wound as we have said until it is healed.
Chapter LXVII.
Of the disorder that occurs in the tendons.
Sometimes there is a rupture in the tendons as we have said, and apply a poultice to the area.
And the surgeons give little cause for concern regarding the intestines; if they do, it is rare; and return them to their proper place at all times.
But if the time is prolonged, there is an adjustment in the cavity where you are placing the intestine; and this occurs due to the extension of the cavity, which is in the tendons as we have said. The cause is that the cavity is stretched, and the area becomes softened and develops into a carbuncle, so apply a poultice.
And the treatment for it is with a cautery as described in the previous narration of it.
And sometimes it is cured by fire according to this manner: and it is that the patient lies on his side between your knees, and soon the place of the rupture of the abscesses dries up by evaporation according to the width as much as three fingers.
And soon strengthen the white cloth that is under the bedsheet once it is uncovered.
And soon take the wick and place it over the area where the cloth is raised, and press it against the belly button.
And soon prick the two raised areas over the end of the wick of the cloth, and adjust one to the other for suturing.
And soon pull the end of the wick out, and do not leave the cloth completely open, nor extend the hole, nor any other cause like this in the treatment of intestinal hernia.
And soon treat that in the treatment of wounds, and after cutting the edges, cleanse it and restore the wound before it is consolidated; for the cloth contracts and the raised area of rupture is not adjusted.
And cautery is better in this place, for it is more conducive to health.
Capitol. lxviii.
Of the mollification of the scrotal skin.
Spots on the scrotal skin in some men are caused by the softening of the tissues between them, and it is believed to be due to excess moisture.
Then it is necessary for the one who is treating such cases to judge when to remove the scrotum according to his skill, and entirely over the softened part of the natural scrotum; and then adjust two flaps at the suturing.
And if you wish, sew in the beginning the excess of the softened scrotum with three or four stitches and a firm suture.
And then incise between the sutures; and afterward, care for the treatment of the other wounds until it is healed and the stitches dissolve.
Chapter LXIX.
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but by cause I am reminded of it in this treatise; and the reminder of it is necessary for two reasons, of which one is so that when a physician is questioned about it, he knows the treatment for those to whom it happens; and the other reason is that we may have occasion to castrate other animals for our young ones, such as bulls, goats, pigs, and similar to animals.
And therefore say that castration is done in two ways: either by excision or by making an incision.
But in that which is done by excision, the way of the operation is to kill the beast in warm water so that its genital parts are softened and relaxed. And then take those out with your hand so that they are resolved and no marks appear upon touch.
In castration performed through incision and extraction, make sure you have the animal and press the cord of the testicles with your left hand.
Then lift the suspensory ligament, and incise over each groove between two processes.
Then incise those glands that you have excoriated. And do not incise any of those on the scrotum for any cause, but incise the thin one which is over the veins.
And this method of castration is better which is performed by traction, for traction firmly leaves no cause of the testicles so that the animal desires copulation.
Then care for the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in males occurs according to two methods: one where there is a streak or appearance that indicates space in the cord of testicles, in which something resembling female characteristics appears on the skin.
And sometimes a flow of urine comes from that vein which is in the cord of the testicles.
In women, it is special: and the vein of the woman around the clitoris is thus like two testicles of a man, a little more round like the scrotum of a man with its two testicles.
And the treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one for women. And you should cut those tight flesh areas where the pain escapes, and then treat those with the cure for other wounds.
And in the second kind for men from which urine comes from the cord of the testicles, neither treatment nor operation is done on it.
Chapter XXI.
On the labia and flesh protruding due to causes in women.
Labia majora tight and firm are placed over natural causes where it is stretched and made lax with a view; sometimes in some women it is enlarged so much that it hangs like in men and expands during intercourse.
Then ensure that you have the phlegm on your hand or a cloth and wipe it off.
And do not finish with a cloth, especially on the sole of the foot, to prevent a flow of pus.
And then proceed with the care and treatment of the wounds until they are healed.
More hidden flesh is flesh that does not appear in the horror of the mother until it fills that space, and a strong cord is tied around the parts outside according to the likeness of the cord (and for this some first called it "caudated evil"); therefore ensure that we cut thus as we cut phlegm, and treat it until it is healed.
Capitol.lix.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Hemorrhoids are when the vein of the woman is perforated, or is slightly inflamed. And it can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to a bad fortune that has preceded, and that is caused either by flesh not fitting well or by a subtle or thick chifac.
It is found in the swelling of the thigh, or in the ribs of the patient, or in the upper part of the abdomen, or in the lower part of the body, and you must prohibit coitus and impregnation and childbirth, and strongly you must prohibit menstruation.
The diagnosis of that is made by observing the midwife, if the obstruction is obvious, palpate carefully; but if it is not obvious, then you examine that with your fingers or by touch.
But if the obstruction is due to a subtle chifac and is close to the two lips, then you separate and dislodge that.
And you place powders on the two lips, and then place your fingers indicating with both hands close by.
And the woman is on her back, her thighs extended, and then spread the two lips forcefully until that subtle chifac is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And then take wool and immerse it in oil and place that over the area, and keep a person there to prevent the incised location from being consolidated.
And if the abscess is large and thick, then you must incise it with a spatula or leaf of mint.
And if the inflammation is due to a carbuncle, then suspend it with a clamp, and incise it.
And use those medicines that stop the flow of venom from a bite, such as mercury chloride, dragon's blood, and ashes, mixed with alum.
And then administer an open lead tube to prevent the wound from being lightly consolidated.
And keep it for a few days and administer boiled water.
And then treat it with the other consolidation remedy once it is healed.
And sometimes accidents occur in the natural abundance of other tissues, then you must incise according to this method. If this is due to an abscessed boil, for the abscessed boil which is in the majority do not let any contrary operation be performed in any manner.
Capitol LXXIII.
For the cure of hemorrhoids and of itch and of red boil that occurs in the groin of women.
Hemorrhoids are appreciated as the result of small veins that constantly bleed within certain areas; and as for old hemorrhoids, they are formed by ulcers.
And I have already said in the division the species of those and the signs of those, and to say likewise which receive treatment and which do not receive treatment.
Therefore, say that hemorrhoids and ulcers when they are in the pelvis and do not appear in the sensation, then for those do not perform any treatment.
But those that are in the openings of the pelvis and on which there is sensation, are those that are cured.
And ensure that you insert the woman into many frictions and then widely extend the thighs with scissors or a rough cloth, and incise those areas with razors.
And then powder the areas where the blood flows from one of the incisive powders over them, doing so as if it were a kiss and with a similar appearance.
And then scrape their feet for an hour, and then immerse that in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then apply that plaster in a decoction of sumac and of roots of millet grass and of squills and with a similar appearance.
And then take flour of orchid and mix it with honey and wine, and make a plaster with this over his back.
And if the blood is incised, that is good; otherwise, apply it to two flax seeds, and to the breasts perform scarification.
And then take wool and immerse it in the juice of fennel or in the juice of centaury or in the juice of hyssop in fermented wine, and apply it to the area; and then dress the area with ointment until it heals.
And cure that which is within and let it be healed.
Chapter 74.
On the perforation of the eye in the vein.
Various special cases of abscesses occurring in the vein, such as cancer, abscesses with hardness, ulcers, adenitis, erythremia, fistulas, gangrene, and other abscesses. And I have already mentioned these illnesses and their special cases, as well as the signs of them, and their treatments in the division.
And see that I mention in this treatise on abscesses how to use the cautery for one that occurs in the vein when it is among the abscesses that heal, and if you want to know how the operation is performed, I will tell you.
Then consider if the pain of the abscess at its beginning is sharp on percussion and fever, and sometimes that it turns red and if there touches over it the sensation, while noting no perforation of it, and cure it with what helps during the maturation until the acuity of the accident ceases.
Then you should place the woman on a pillow that has two parts; recline her upper body and adjust her legs to the part beyond the abdomen, and spread her thighs apart. Place her hands over her hips, and support her knees with your hands. Liaise the quascus with liament as needed.
Then the midwife should follow along the rectum straight and administer the instrument through which the opening of the uterus has been opened, the shape of which will be described in the causes that will be given soon.
When you want to administer this instrument, place it along the lower part of the uterus of the woman, and what part of the instrument enters the uterus should not be more than the lower part of the uterus and push through the malaise. If the instrument is larger than the size of the fist, then cover it with powder on the surface of the fist so that the instrument cannot enter the space of the fist.
Cover the fluid that flows in the blade of the lancet above and ensure that the minister holds the blade and rotates the fluid until the pores of the fist are opened.
And when the excitement appears, and it is touched with the hand and becomes hot and moist, then cover that part by applying a cold compress to the head with spit from the lancet.
And when the phlegm is evacuated, then cover the wound with a sponge submerged in olive oil or green oil in which there is some astringency; and place the wick in the area of the fist.
And place over the fist and on the woollen cloth submerged in water in which mallows are boiled.
And it is usually cured in about two days by applying ointment which you apply while it is healing.
And sometimes the liver and wound are washed with an ointment made of honey and vinegar, then immersed in water in which lemon or aromatic herbs have been boiled, and then returned to the ointment.
And if the wound is inside the liver and hardened, then carefully observe that you refrain from treating it with force, taking care as we have said in the division.
Chapter 75.
To teach midwives how to properly treat bruises when they occur in an unnatural manner.
Necessary cause is that the midwife know at the beginning the figure of a natural birth by signs, and when you see the woman expressing herself at the openings and desiring to smell the air, and being refreshed by what is over her, and hastening the emergence of the bruise, then you can perceive that this part is according to the natural figure, and its emergence is over her head, and the second one is either at or suspended below the navel.
When you see those signs, then hold the patient's abdomen so that the fetus descends slightly; when it is on its head, place the second stage, and this is purified from those superfluities through good purification.
That which is another from this part is unnatural and unacceptable, for when the fetus is situated on its feet and the body of the patient is situated in front of the head of the patient and its feet, or one of its hands, or at its foot, or the head of the patient and its hand, or its abdomen, and strongly it is turned over its own neck, resembling unacceptably the figures of the patient.
For necessary causes, the midwife must be wise and subtle in all those causes, and she must guard against error and deception.
And I show all the figures of those, and what each organ is in them so that it is significant and placed there.
When the pain is situated on its head by natural accident, and it is violent for the woman and made to her part difficult, and sometimes the virtue of her already weakened, then apply that sezer, or what women have her, and evaporate the concoction with fenugreek and with humid oils.
And then insert the probe between his so-called small spout and open the second one, or dry that one with its joint inside where flows what is within it of moisture. And press the woman's abdomen so that the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then cause the woman to be anointed with almond oil and fennel oil.
And then command him, by the Christ, that he be immersed in warm water and make him sneeze by blowing into him; and keep his mouth and nose closed for about an hour, until the fetus comes out quickly.
And if the two parts of the fetus are already expelled at the beginning, then cause you to reduce them gradually for facilitation. But if you do not obey the instrument, then place the woman on a cushion and lift her feet off it, and quickly hold the cushion over the ground; and make sure the woman does not fall due to the concussion.
And if the hands are not turned inside and the wound is not closed, then incise there and extract the fragments of the wound or lay the body on your cloth and extract that equally, for that will be thoroughly cleaned.
When the wound extends over its feet, then scrape those parts within it, and soon make the wound smaller, and soon cover it, and soon take a piece of it and extend those parts little by little.
More when it extends into the thighs, then command him to express it, and do that externally in conditions, for it will be thoroughly cleaned if God wills.
And if it is not thoroughly cleaned as we have recommended, then return the wound little by little until you cover it according to the natural figure, for it will then be thoroughly cleaned with slight scraping.
And if all that we have recommended is prohibited, then take a mixture of alum and dissolved gum, and pound it thoroughly in the mortar for good pounding, and line it with the inside of the woman's skin, the lower part of her abdomen. And then make that cut in clear water, once you reach the hypochondria.
And when you see that the parts around it have become numbed, then perform a mirtle fumigation on it and place your hand over it. And when you have performed the fumigation for an hour, then make that incision over a basin, and immediately perform that snuffing and extend the mouth of it, and remove it, and apply a light compression to the lower part of the abdomen, which will cause the wound to soon become almost unnoticeable.
Suture the wound longitudinally with one of their hands. Support the hand of the patient in reduction, but if you cannot reduce it, then elevate the woman and make her stand.
And if standing does not help, then apply the jazer to the wound, and shake the patient's thighs with vigorous concussion, and then administer liniments which you prepare from mucilages.
And if the childbirth has come, then apply the sizer over cloth, and then study the reduction of the hand, and close the wound according to its natural figure, and make the woman cough and command her to hold herself while the wound is not forgotten.
Lift the patient's leg wide and extend their hand while stretching the foot surface towards the thigh. Have the midwife hold the patient's hand and gently rotate the small part little by little, so that it becomes easier to facilitate.
And when it is equalized, then place over the wound what we have recommended of oil and ointments.
And then command that a small amount of warm water be given little by little. When you have done this, place the compress on a cloth and command that it be inclined over the right side, and then command that it be well wrung out; and make the compress moisten with condiment. The fetus's exit is prepared on the side.
When the horrices of the mother occur according to this manner, consider it, and then incise the second one with your finger so that it is evacuated of moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended over the face and neck of the mother, then incise the one that is causing the obstruction, so that it is not retained and causes harm.
And then push the fetus into the parts inside where you place that according to what fits, and order the woman to strain herself several times, and it will be easily delivered by gentle pressure, if God wills.
The exit of twins or many fetuses. Know that twins or spots of many fetuses are naturally born, and sometimes nine or ten, but more than this is strange and needs to be investigated. Yet the causes are mostly natural, not supernatural.
And concerning these, whether they be multiplied, one second, and are separated by ciphac, distinguish those within the ligament in the navel of each. Sometimes they are easily delivered as if one fetus by natural passage, and some remain for several times through an unmanageable delivery as we have reported.
And if they are difficult, some of them you should induce labor and proceed to what we have said about unnatural figures, then you treat those as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does what she does with ease and subtlety, and with delay, and be ingenious according to all figures as prepared by her leading to health.
Remembrance of that which is formed in the matrix from embryos and are aborted.
Some pregnancies are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more up to ten. You must verify that a woman who aborts has borne one, another all of them formed, the cause of which is made by the measurement of the glorious sages.
And all this covers what is in the science of the midwife, for she must attend to it carefully, and then place her hand on it so that it is proper.
Capitol.lix.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat the dead fetus where we have said in the division of medicine and it is not outside the body, then you must use surgery manually. You must consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and is not among those conditions for which her life is feared to be endangered.
When the woman is laid on her back with her head inclined sideways and her thighs elevated.
And the minister should hold that [part] with two hands or tie it to the surface so that the body does not extend during the extraction.
And then moisten the mouth of the patient with olive oil and honey and juice from alfalfa and flaxseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and honey, and place her hand with facilitation on the patient, and seek with her hand the location where the fingers will enter the wound.
And place the fingers accordingly: then consider if the wound is prepared to close over its own edges, and then place the fingers in the folds of the skin, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or let the beard be, or on the collarbone, or on the proper locations of the ribs, or let the hypochondria be.
But if the descent is on his feet, then at the ankle, or in the middle of the back.
And make sure that the thumb is with the right hand, and curve it at that location which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand with ease and place the thumb in one of those locations which we have said, until he reaches the underlying cause.
And then place and hold another thumb, or the third if necessary, so that it is an equal counter-pressure, and not extension according to its straightness solely.
And let it be held in all parts, so that the pressure of it may be alleviated as is done in extracting a tooth.
And make sure that the extension is softened; and if any part of it is retained, then let the midwife anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them expertly and rotate them where the retention occurs.
Then if the part of the fetus is left out, let the fingers enter where it may be pushed in; and do so until all the fetus is expelled.
But if the hand is placed in front of the other, and it is not possible to reduce it due to the constriction, then cover that part with a cloth; and extract it until all is expelled, and incise it at the junction of the hand or near the elbow.
And do the same with the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or it experiences constriction during extraction, or there is fluid in its head, then you must insert a pair of forceps between the fingers and cut open the head to drain the fluid, or use an instrument called "alundat" to remove it, the shape of which will be shown in the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
And similarly, if the fetus has a naturally large head: then you must incise it with a gematius knife, or use an alundat instrument as we have said; and extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is swollen and compressed, you should open the furcifer, when the humidity from the feet has infiltrated.
And if it is not complicated, nor swollen, then you incise the head as soon as it suits you.
And if the abscesses of the abdomen are suppurated or in it, then make sure you perforate it where the humidity is present.
And if the fistula is on their feet, then the traction of it is light and the direction towards the mouth of the major vessel is light.
And if it is swollen, you should incise the abdomen and feet, when you extract that piece of cloth which you have wrapped around your hand, and incise the abdomen and feet where the fluid flows.
And if the other members are reduced and the head returns, then the surgeon should insert his left hand; and if the mouth of the major vessel is opened, then he should insert his hand into the groin, and seek out the head, and throw that into the fingers into the mouth of the major vessel, and quickly insert one or two fingers, and pull them out with those.
And if the mouth of the main vein is constricted by an abscess, when it happens to someone, then make sure it is not treated excessively; rather, administer an effusion of fatty humid causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fistula is on the side of the body, then it should be punctured if possible: and what we have said about the living fistula should be administered.
And if this is not possible, then incise in pieces, and extract it.
And make sure you do not leave any cause inside the second incision.
And when you have completed your operation, then administer what we have said about the cure for abscesses caused by an abscess of the main vein.
And if there is a flux of blood, then apply cold waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in her womb where one child was dead, and near that fire another pregnancy had begun, and the fire is dead for the other. It happens that after a long time a boil appears on the arm; and it swells up into an open sore, and begins to discharge pus.
And I was called to treat it, and medicated it for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
Then I placed my hand on it using strong adhesive plaster, and pressed with one bone, and after some days, pressed with another bone; and I was too amazed, for in the abdomen there is no bone.
And then I realized that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
Then I incised the wound, and extracted the bones of the dead fetus, the woman having been in her abdominal convulsions for a long time, and had already miscarried in this manner many times, and cured her of a small arm complaint.
And I do not refuse it because it is strange, but rather because in this there is science and aid to what the physician provides through treatment.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the stone.
Form of vertigo at which the liver is opened:

And let the width of each wire be as wide as two fingers, and the margin on both sides be as wide as one finger. The length of each is a palm and a half; and in the middle location between two wires are two adjustments of that same sized wire which are already fastened, the length of which is about a palm and a bit more, and the width of each is as wide as two fingers, or a bit more.
And these two additions should be inserted in the mouth of the womb so that they are open when you rotate the two prescribed virtues.
Form another one similar to that, very subtle and light:
Make it of fine linen or of wool according to the likeness of forceps. However, at the extremity of each, there are two additions as you see, and the length of those additions is about one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.

For the treatment of an unperforated anal condition.
When the child is born and the anus is not perforated, which have already been treated with a fine ligature. Then have the midwife perforate with her said ligature; otherwise, perforate it with a sharp needle, and take care that it does not touch the membrane.
And place warm wool in oil and wine over it; then apply ointment to it while it is warm.
But if you fear it is ligated, then insert a cannula for several days, and wait until the child wants to defecate.

For the treatment of fistulas that discharge pus.
The fistulas that discharge low pus are often large, and those that discharge similarly are near the buttocks or in the space of one side.
And it is either a fistula or a boil.
And when that infection is old and flows from watery white moisture or subtle suppuration, sometimes these are from such fistulas, some penetrating.
And those that penetrate are known by what happens from them through the discharge and by wind condition; sometimes the patient uses the site of discharge, and a strong smell is emitted from such boils.
And from some of these fistulas, sometimes the penetration occurs into the bladder, and into the flesh of the groin; and from those that penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the notch of the hip.
And to determine whether a penetrating fistula goes into the buttocks or not, you should insert your finger into the buttock, and introduce a thin probe of reed or iron into the fistula when there is no pus.
If there is hardness, then insert a thin probe of lead or horse hair into that probe feeling the thread or the hair in your hand.
And if you do not feel that at all, nor proceed from any cause of excretion, worm, or hardness, as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrable, and now your treatment is complete.
And when the fistula is penetrable into the bladder or into the flesh of the penis, then the significance of this is dysuria from that side and prohibition thereof until the area with medicine is consolidated.
And if it is penetrable into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the circuit, then the sign of this is that the probe passes through here if there is no hardness in the bone, and pain in the circuit of the affected area; and that it remains red for some time; and that it does not respond to this treatment, nor is it consolidated with ointment.
And in all those penetrable fistulas, complete cure is not achieved, and the cure of these requires the labor and skill of the surgeons over which they preside.
In those that are not penetrating and not ancient, cure with iron is hoped for according to what I will recount to you, and what already exists and precedes.
And it is that the patient lies on his back and elevates his legs between his hands, the thighs inclined towards the abdomen of the patient, and then insert a lead or iron tube, if it is in the tortuous fistula, into the place where the patient feels the pain.
And if the patient feels the pain around the throat, then you must insert the thumb in the throat.
And if you feel the pain in your thumb already by itself clearly penetrating, or something between your thumb and that siphon or flesh, then you can be certain that it is penetrating; and then do not work on that, for there is no cure there, as we have said.
But however, some say that it is cured in some men after the third day.

Of the section on worms generated under the skin and called the bovine illness.
This illness is named in some lands the bovine disease. And it is feared because of its malice, for when it goes in the body and rises to the head, and reaches the vein, then greatly inflames it and enters and destroys the vein, and this frequently occurs.

Of the section on the illness of the nafir.
This disease is called nafir in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in some parts of the body, and often is transmitted from one part to another.
And I have already seen that which I will recount to you. I have been called to a sick woman in a village, and examined her arm where I found a small swelling in the vein network of the arm. After it had risen for about an hour, I observed that this swelling went up like vermilion, though less intensely than feared, as if it were living silver moving from place to place.
And then I noted the pain in that area and placed a compress on the muscle, and there it stayed for about an hour.
And then I moved to the other side of the body where I applied it to the other arm.
And then I was told that she should move her body all over; and it was too marvelous to see the change in her and the speed with which the pain moved from one part of the body to another. And I had already seen this before in my hands according to that manner, but I have seen many cases where it is found that pain is permuted from one limb to another. But not all have such heels as in the female.
And I do not consider it to be so, but rather that it is because the female had a thin body and exposed veins, and in this appearance there is a sensation of that swelling changed.
And it is necessary that this backward curvature not appear in those who are delicate and have soft, engorged veins.
And when you want the cure for it, and the patient feels that pain, if it does not appear on the heel as we have said, then strengthen that area and let it be slightly and gently over that until the swollen swelling is inserted, and cauterize the place.
But if you do not see it on the heel, then cure that by excess of the body and by what you expel of swelling, and administer those that stink in pills and those of serapie and similar.
From the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are diverse according to the species, and according to the places of the body in which they occur; for their diversity is that some have large points, small, concave, and blunt, being solid; and some have three angles, and of those to which belong tongues, and of those to which belong feathers.
And of the signs of the arrow is when it strikes the skull, which is above the brain, for it happens through the intense and violent pain, scotoma, vertigo, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile, and there is a white moisture in the area of the wound resembling dust, and from it appears like an excess of flesh.
And therefore if you see these signs, then abstain from the cure and extraction of the arrow, unless it is outside.
